  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<span id="freeTextContainer5971911592032953182"><i>I am tired of being used, hurt, and cast aside.</i><br/><br/><b>Adelina Amouteru is a survivor of the blood fever.</b> A decade ago, the deadly illness swept through her nation.   <span id="freeText5971911592032953182" style="display:none"><i>I am tired of being used, hurt, and cast aside.</i><br /><br /><b>Adelina Amouteru is a survivor of the blood fever.</b> A decade ago, the deadly illness swept through her nation. Most of the infected perished, while many of the children who survived were left with strange markings. Adelina’s black hair turned silver, her lashes went pale, and now she has only a jagged scar where her left eye once was. Her cruel father believes she is a malfetto, an abomination, ruining their family’s good name and standing in the way of their fortune. But some of the fever’s survivors are rumored to possess more than just scars—they are believed to have mysterious and powerful gifts, and though their identities remain secret, they have come to be called the Young Elites.<br /><br /><b>Teren Santoro works for the king.</b> As Leader of the Inquisition Axis, it is his job to seek out the Young Elites, to destroy them before they destroy the nation. He believes the Young Elites to be dangerous and vengeful, but it’s Teren who may possess the darkest secret of all. <br /><br /><b>Enzo Valenciano is a member of the Dagger Society.</b> This secret sect of Young Elites seeks out others like them before the Inquisition Axis can. But when the Daggers find Adelina, they discover someone with powers like they’ve never seen. <br /><br />Adelina wants to believe Enzo is on her side, and that Teren is the true enemy. But the lives of these three will collide in unexpected ways, as each fights a very different and personal battle. But of one thing they are all certain: Adelina has abilities that shouldn’t belong in this world. A vengeful blackness in her heart. And a desire to destroy all who dare to cross her.<br /><br /><i>It is my turn to use. My turn to hurt.</i></span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1078046955" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1078046955" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1078046955?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1078046955" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5162693338001394600"><blockquote>
  <i>I know who you really are. Who will ever want you, Adelina?<br/><br/>My fury heightens. Everyone. They will cower at my feet, and I will make them bleed.</i>
</blockquote><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1413598931ra/11535645.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Two words. <b>Fuck, yeah!</b><br/><br/>I don't even know how to describe this book. Maybe <b>William Shakespeare's <i>Mistborn</i></b>? It is not without its flaws, but the love of a book, much like the love of a human, is completely chemistry-based, and for me, this book just <i>clicked.</i> Every so often, the planets align, and Khanh completely loves a book. It happens!<br/><br/>This book has so</span>
  <span id="freeText5162693338001394600" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>I know who you really are. Who will ever want you, Adelina?<br><br>My fury heightens. Everyone. They will cower at my feet, and I will make them bleed.</i>
</blockquote><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1413598931ra/11535645.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Two words. <b>Fuck, yeah!</b><br><br>I don't even know how to describe this book. Maybe <b>William Shakespeare's <i>Mistborn</i></b>? It is not without its flaws, but the love of a book, much like the love of a human, is completely chemistry-based, and for me, this book just <i>clicked.</i> Every so often, the planets align, and Khanh completely loves a book. It happens!<br><br>This book has so many elements that I love. A <b>very light romance.</b> A dark, <b>physically-scarred main character.</b> A beautiful (and completely <b>platonic</b>) friendship between the main female character and a <b>male courtesan</b>. A complex <b>"villain"</b>. And a plot to <b>take over the kingdom</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1413338469ra/11498671.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Can I get a <b>"Fuck, yeah?"</b><br><br><u>The Summary</u>: <blockquote>
  <i>You tried to escape from me, he says, but I found you. You have lost and I have won. I tell him that I’m glad he’s dead. I tell him to go away. But he stays.<br>It doesn’t matter, anyway. I’m going to die tomorrow morning</i>
</blockquote><b>Adelina Amouteru is a murderer</b>, justified. Adelina has a shitty life. She is like Cinderella, without the stepmother, but with a father like hers, who needs a wicked stepmother? There is only one word to describe daddy, and that word is <b>motherfucking asshole.</b> Ok, make that two words. Whatever.<br><br>Anyway, it is a pretty shitty life mainly because not so long ago, this fever thing swept through her country, killing massive amounts of people, leaving the rest physically scarred. Adelina herself is not exempt. Not only that, there is the mental scarring, the <b>stigma</b> of being a <b>
  <i>malfetto</i>
</b>. <i>Malfettos</i> are feared, hated, shunned. Their very existence puts shame onto a family name. Adelina's family, formerly wealthy and respected, now suffers from her disgrace. Because she lived. And sadly, her fate is far better than some...there have been <b>rumors that the <i>malfetto</i> are cursed</b>, as such, they have been badly persecuted.<br><br>It could be worse for Adelina, but not by much. Her dad hates her. Her sister is blissfully under her dad's thumb. And now her dad is going to sell her off to be a nasty old man's wife. What's a girl to do? Run away! And when daddy catches her and cruelly forces her hand? <b>Kill him!</b><blockquote>
  <i>I am Adelina Amouteru, the phantoms whispered to my father, speaking my most frightening thoughts in a chorus of voices, dripping with hatred. My hatred. I belong to no one. On this night, I swear to you that I will rise above everything you’ve ever taught me. I will become a force that this world has never known. I will come into such power that none will dare hurt me again.</i>
</blockquote>And that, my friends, is how Adelina becomes a murderer. Totally justified. <b>You go, girl! Way to self-defense!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1413598718ra/11535608.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Only she is caught. Sadface. And she is sentenced to be executed. Even more sadface. Only at the last minute (it's always the last minute, isn't it?!) she is saved. Not that she needed much saving. I mean, look at this shit. Girl's got it under control, yo! Then she faints. Totally excusable, I mean, <i>look at that shit.</i> <blockquote>
  <i>And just like that, the black clouds twist—they scatter into a swarm of a million moving flecks that swirl across the sky and then dive down, down, down at the crowd. A nightmare of locusts. They descend on us with merciless efficiency, their buzzing drowning out the people’s cries.</i>
</blockquote>That takes a lot of energy. Maybe an entire package of Oreo's worth of energy. Can't blame a girl for fainting after that.<br><br>Next thing Adelina knows, she wakes up in this totally plush place, handsome stranger rescuer dude is there, and he's in a Super Secret Special Society called <b>The Young Elites.</b> Only it's not just ANYONE. This guy, <b>Enzo</b> is the <b>crown prince</b>!<blockquote>
  <i>The word was that he had nearly died from the blood fever. He came out of it marked instead. Unfit to be heir to the throne. Enzo’s older sister stripped Enzo of his crown and banished him permanently from the palace, never again to set foot near the royal family.</i>
</blockquote>Kind of. Not really. That's because, <b>he, too, is a <i>malfetto</i></b>, and since the public has been told that <i>malfettoes</i> are BAD EVIL NO GOOD, it would be kind of problematic to put one of those people on the throne, right? So his uncle, the King...is not fond of the prince, to put it lightly.<br><br><b>And now the prince wants his throne back.</b> WHAT DO??! TAKE OVER THE WORLD. Or the country, at least. Baby steps! Today, the country. Tomorrow, the universe.<br><br>So the <i>malfettoes</i> are a potentially powerful bunch. The trouble is that <i>malfettoes</i> are aplenty, but only a few of them have special powers. <b>Is Adelina one of the select ones?</b> Yes. But can she actually control her abilities? Can she <b>pass the Young Elites' test?</b><br><br>The price for failure is high.<blockquote>
  <i> If for some reason I can’t control my abilities, they won’t just cast me out of the Dagger Society. I know too much. A weak link in a world that wants us dead. That weak link could be me.<br>If I cannot pass their tests, then they will do to me what they must have done with the boy who could not control the rain. They will kill me.</i>
</blockquote><u>The Setting</u>: I do believe the best word for this setting is <b>plush.</b> It has a very Renaissance Italy feel to it, and there is plenty of bling. The main character is rescued from a somewhat poor existence and boosted into the lap of luxury. The setting is oftentimes luxurious. There are secret lairs. And there are pretty pretty dresses and I DON'T EVEN CARE. I loved it all.<br><br><b>The Characters</b>: How do I love them? Let me count the ways. There are no heroes and heroines in this book, <b>only anti-heroes</b>, and I'll be damned if I didn't love them.<br><br><u>Adelina</u>:<blockquote>
  <i>As I stare silently back, I feel something powerful stir inside me—a buried fire, subdued during childhood and long forgotten. I have lived all my life in the shadow of my father and my sister. Now that I’m standing in the sun for the first time, I dare to think differently.<br>The broken butterfly has been made whole.</i>
</blockquote>I love a <b>strong, dark, bitter, angry character (who's not afraid to kill)</b>, and I can only describe Adelina as <b>totally kick-ass</b>. She has a darkness inside her that I love, and she is physically scarred, which I also love. Adelina is missing an eye. She is good-looking, but the book never makes it overwhelming. She has doubts, she has fears. She is haunted by the ghost of her own guilt.<blockquote>
  <i> I do this because I love you, my father’s ghost whispers. You may not understand it right now, but it is for your own good. You are a monster. I still love you. I will set you right.</i>
</blockquote>She has worries about her own self-worth.<blockquote>
  <i>They are only good to me because they need me. Just like Enzo. Kindness with strings attached. Would they have befriended me if I were worthless?</i>
</blockquote>She is not afraid to get revenge. <b>Adelina is no pussy-ass weakling female character</b>, and that is the most important thing. I also absolutely love her relationship with her sister.<br><br><b>Enzo</b>: <blockquote>
  <i>“I will take back my throne soon,” Enzo whispers. “And malfettos will no longer live in fear.”</i>
</blockquote>The man with the plan. The Boy Who Would Be King. He wants his birthright, and he'll go through anything to get it. Adelina be damned. His romance with her...is it a romance?<blockquote>
  <i>“She is nothing to me,” he snaps with a careless gesture of one hand. “Nothing more than a Dagger recruit. Just part of our plans.” The ice in his voice hits me hard. Nothing more. A rip appears on my heart.</i>
</blockquote>Is it love, or manipulation? There is only one goal here. Enzo may have a noble purpose...but he is no saint. He can kill with the best of them, and don't you <i>dare</i> cross his friend.<blockquote>
  <i>The next morning, Inquisitors find Count Maurizio Saldana’s dismembered body nailed to his front door, his mouth suspended in a scream, his corpse burned black beyond recognition.</i>
</blockquote><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1413598921ra/11535644.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Teren</b>: <blockquote>
  <i>He kneels on the floor. Lifts the whip. Holds his breath. Then he snaps the whip over his head. The blades rake deep into the flesh of his back, ripping jagged lines across his skin. He lets out a strangled gasp as pain floods him, robbing him of his breath. <br>I am a deformed creature, he mouths silently, repeating the words he once said as a twelve-year-old boy, an Inquisitorin-training, kneeling before the sixteen-year-old Princess Giulietta.</i>
</blockquote>Mad, obsessive, worshipful love. Teren is alternately a pitiful and terrifying creature. He has been in love with beautiful young queen all his life, he is utterly devoted to her. He will do anything for her, including <b>find and destroy Adelina Amouteru</b>, using any tactic possible, however dirty.<blockquote>
  <i>“You have three days,” he says in a low voice. “If you go back on your word again, I will shoot an arrow through your sister’s neck and out the back of her skull. She’ll be lucky if that’s the first thing I do.” He smiles, his teeth flashing in the night.</i>
</blockquote>Talk about evil! Talk about madness for love. Talk about a low-sense of self-worth! Enzo, the evil guard, is the "villain," of this book, if it has one. He is so filled with self-loathing.<br><br><u>Rafaelle</u>: Probably my favorite character, to be honest. How rare is it that one finds a beautiful amale character in a platonic, true friendship with a female character. And beautiful he is. <blockquote>
  <i></i>
</blockquote>Daaaaaamn, son!<blockquote>
  <i>His hair, black and shining, drapes across one of his shoulders in a loose, silken braid. His olive skin is smooth, flawless, glowing. The faint musk of night lilies envelops him in a veil, intoxicating, promising something forbidden.</i>
</blockquote>I like him because he's pretty. I like him because he is a <b>male courtesan</b>. I like him because he wants a better life, and he has a kind, gentle heart. Beautiful boy!<br><br>This book. Can I get a FUCK YEAH?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1413598850ra/11535631.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="5162693338001394600" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_794189448" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/794189448" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/794189448?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer794189448" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12637451111709506728"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413010780i/11455692.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Want to know what happens when Marie Lu does darker and sexier? <br/><br/><b>
  <u>Then read this book.</u>
</b><br/><br/>Contrary to what I first believed, this book is not dystopian or post-apocalyptic, but is actually a dark fantasy set in a bleak world full of magic, complex villains and princes looking to reclaim their throne. And it's damn good.<br/><br/>Adelina Amouteru is a survivor of a blood fever that swept through her nation when she was a child. The fever left only a few survivors and those survivors remained permanently scar</span>
  <span id="freeText12637451111709506728" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413010780i/11455692.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Want to know what happens when Marie Lu does darker and sexier? <br><br><b>
  <u>Then read this book.</u>
</b><br><br>Contrary to what I first believed, this book is not dystopian or post-apocalyptic, but is actually a dark fantasy set in a bleak world full of magic, complex villains and princes looking to reclaim their throne. And it's damn good.<br><br>Adelina Amouteru is a survivor of a blood fever that swept through her nation when she was a child. The fever left only a few survivors and those survivors remained permanently scarred with strange markings on their bodies. But some of them were left with something else... strange abilities that made them powerful, dangerous and feared. These people are called The Young Elites. Adelina discovers her own unique abilities in unfortunate circumstances and is propelled into a world where everyone, it seems, is an enemy.<br><br><b>I absolutely loved Adelina.</b><br><br><i>“I am Adelina Amouteru. I belong to no one. On this night, I swear to you that I will rise above everything you’ve ever taught me. I will become a force that this world has never known. I will come into such power that none will dare hurt me again.”</i><br><br>She's spent her whole life being abused by her father, feeling unloved and worthless. And she has a complex relationship with her sister - while she loves her dearly, she's always been jealous of the way their father was affectionate towards her. Her life moves from one hurdle to the next; when she finally unleashes the power she needs to stand up to her father, this makes her an enemy of society.<br><br><b>Enter the Young Elites.</b><br><br>There are so many fascinating characters in this novel. Obviously readers will love the extremely sexy (but not sexually graphic) scenes between Adelina and Enzo, the leader of the Elites, but there are many other interesting dynamics going on. I especially loved the relationship between Adeline and Raffaele; it's so rare to see a platonic relationship between a young male and female told well, particularly when the guy is described as "beautiful".<br><br>But I think the thing I like best about this book is how no one is simply good or bad, everything is much more complicated and interesting than that. Adelina is allowed to have her own dark, twisted thoughts. She's not a hero. She's broken, selfish and even a little wicked at times:<br><br><i>“In spite of everything, I feel a strange sense of glee.<br>All this chaos is of my own creation.”</i><br><br>And every few chapters, the evil Teren is given his own perspective for several pages that gives us insight into why he behaves the way he does. I never liked him, of course, but I did feel a strange sense of sympathy for him. <b>Aren't complex villains just one of the best things ever?</b><br><br>So Adelina gets caught between two powerful groups of people who could each make her life hell, simply take it away from her, or hurt the sister she loves. She must learn fast, keep secrets and trust no one... it's a wild, breathless journey that had me thanking the god of literature that this is going to be a series. I can't wait to see what happens next.<br><br><i>“Everyone has darkness inside them, however hidden.”</i><br><br><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCcVsMUSAzMlIKs3nw-xe_nw" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12637451111709506728" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1213573873" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1213573873" />
    <a title="Christine Riccio" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10093827-christine-riccio"><img alt="Christine Riccio" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533739122p2/10093827.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1213573873?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christine Riccio" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christine Riccio" href="/user/show/10093827-christine-riccio">Christine Riccio</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1213573873" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1880859112674678443">I grew to enjoy this book! At first I was hesitant, but the darkness of the characters eventually sucked me in and I will definitely be reading book 2.     <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2637303224?book_show_action=true">Dec 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780147511683" href="/book/show/24611432-the-young-elites">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2637303224" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1850068510673833785">i love marie lu, so i had no idea i could love her more than i already did. but i honestly think this is my favourite book (and potentially series) she has written. its dark, twisted, powerful, and it surprised me in so many ways. <br/><br/>her other two series have either a sci-fi or dystopian feel to them, with both taking place in the future. so assumed this would be similar - imagine my intrigue when i realised the story takes place in renaissance italy?! i am totally on board with that. i just wish t</span>
  <span id="freeText1850068510673833785" style="display:none">i love marie lu, so i had no idea i could love her more than i already did. but i honestly think this is my favourite book (and potentially series) she has written. its dark, twisted, powerful, and it surprised me in so many ways. <br /><br />her other two series have either a sci-fi or dystopian feel to them, with both taking place in the future. so assumed this would be similar - imagine my intrigue when i realised the story takes place in renaissance italy?! i am totally on board with that. i just wish there was more world-building. its pretty basic, with only short references to the blood fever here and there. i really wanted more exploration within the setting because i find it so interesting. <br /><br />but even though the world building is a little weak, the character development is amazing! everyone is just so complex - its refreshing to read about characters with so much depth to them. and gahhh. im so in love with enzo. &lt;3 also, i will say that i dont quite like adelina. i just cant quite connect with her, but i think thats why im so excited to see how her character develops. my lack of attachment makes it easy for me to be okay with the direction her story arc is taking. its going to be so much fun to watch her take down everything and everyone in her way. i really hope the story gets much darker in the next books, because i am ready for a bloodbath of revenge. so bring it on!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4.5 stars</i></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="1850068510673833785" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_628711136" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/628711136" />
    <a title="Angelica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16201093-angelica"><img alt="Angelica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507050077p2/16201093.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/628711136?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angelica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angelica" href="/user/show/16201093-angelica">Angelica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=authors-i-love">authors-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=first-in-series">first-in-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=release-2014">release-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=awesome-heroines">awesome-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=disappointment">disappointment</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=great-ending">great-ending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=super-powers">super-powers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer628711136" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17122279756586432478"><b>This was... disappointing?</b><br/><br/>It feels weird writing this negative review when everyone I know is absolutely raving about it. It makes me feel like maybe, I missed something. I even debated rounding up the rating or letting go of some of my issues with the novel but that would just wouldn't be me. <br/><br/>So, here's the honesty.<br/><br/><b>I went into this book with the highest of all the hopes. I finished it feeling entirely unfulfilled. </b><br/><br/>First let me say that this was a very interesting book to read after reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13638125.Vicious__Villains___1_' title='Vicious (Villains, #1) by V.E. Schwab' rel='nofollow noopener'>Vici</a></span>
  <span id="freeText17122279756586432478" style="display:none"><b>This was... disappointing?</b><br /><br />It feels weird writing this negative review when everyone I know is absolutely raving about it. It makes me feel like maybe, I missed something. I even debated rounding up the rating or letting go of some of my issues with the novel but that would just wouldn't be me. <br /><br />So, here's the honesty.<br /><br /><b>I went into this book with the highest of all the hopes. I finished it feeling entirely unfulfilled. </b><br /><br />First let me say that this was a very interesting book to read after reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13638125.Vicious__Villains___1_" title="Vicious (Villains, #1) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Vicious</a> by V.E. Schwab. <br /><br />In both books, everyone has their own morally ambiguous motives and everyone is determined to achieve their sometimes destructive goals. <br /><br />Just like Vicious, this book follows the lives of characters that have gained natural powers through sickness and death. Some see their characters as holy, some see them as things that must be destroyed. <br /><br />There are characters in both books that fill the same positions. For example, in both, there is a man hunting down the protagonists, in hopes to kill them all. This man does this because he believes it is the will of God. This man, Eli in Vicious and Teren in TYE, even has the same power in both books! <br /><br />There are a lot of other minor similarities that I'm not going to go into because despite what they had in common, I consider these to be very different books. It's just that unfortunately, having read them back to back, probably caused me to not enjoy this one quite as much. <br /><br />At least, that's the excuse I'm giving this book.<br /><br /><b>My main issue with this novel was that I simply didn't care all that much about it. </b>I didn't care much for the characters, which all blended in my mind after a while. I didn't care for the plot, which stalled in the middle and made the pacing feel off. I didn't care for the world-building which was just a renaissance painting world with superpowers. I just didn't care. <br /><br />I would put this book down and forget to pick it back up. I wouldn't feel any desire to truly get back into it. I felt pretty <i>meh</i> about the whole reading experience.<br /><br />I feel like I wanted more than I got. I wanted more because I expected more. That said, I really liked the end, and not because it was over! I liked it because it was everything I had expected the entire novel to be. <br /><br /><b>In the end, despite my disappointment, I am actually looking forward to the sequel.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="17122279756586432478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1076348103" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1076348103" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1076348103?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=secrets">secrets</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=strong-heroine">strong-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=betrayal">betrayal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=spies">spies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=family">family</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1076348103" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7520876208118036117"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1412913111i/11441217._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='450' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Adelina definitely surprised me.</b> <br/><br/>She's such a strong heroine. The kind we just <i>love</i> to have in our fantasy reads. It’s pretty crazy, to say, how easily she and I clicked. Turns out, even though I don’t believe myself to enjoy or, sometimes, <em>want</em> to hurt people, we have many things in common, such as fighting for what is dear to us, family and always trying our best.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1412912568i/11441117.jpg' width='400' height='350' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Enzo is the love-interest of Adelina. He is the rightful heir to the throne, but was banned, since he is a <em>malfetto</em> and <em>malfettos</em> ar</span>
  <span id="freeText7520876208118036117" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1412913111i/11441217._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="450" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Adelina definitely surprised me.</b> <br><br>She's such a strong heroine. The kind we just <i>love</i> to have in our fantasy reads. It’s pretty crazy, to say, how easily she and I clicked. Turns out, even though I don’t believe myself to enjoy or, sometimes, <em>want</em> to hurt people, we have many things in common, such as fighting for what is dear to us, family and always trying our best.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1412912568i/11441117.jpg" width="400" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Enzo is the love-interest of Adelina. He is the rightful heir to the throne, but was banned, since he is a <em>malfetto</em> and <em>malfettos</em> are feared and, even, in some other places killed. Just because they’re different from others. They may not be ‘evil’ but, to the eyes of others, they very likely are since they are usually flawed and have unique powers. Enzo is the head of the <em>Young Elites</em> which is a secret sect of <i>malfettos</i> who are organizing…something big. They want to make of Enzo the ruler of the Kingdom. Which is fantastic. I think it to be a great idea…except that there wasn’t much they actually did to achieve their goal.<br><br>In fact, there wasn’t that much happening in the story. It mostly revolves around Adelina who became a spy, in order to free her sister, Violetta, from the hands of Teren, someone who despises <i>malfettos</i>. I do understand why Adelina decided to agree to Teren’s terms for the freedom of her dear sister, but I think the whole concept and situation was too simple, in a way. There was a <i>lot lot lot</i> of potential but it feels, to me, like the author somehow decided to take the easiest path, because of how she ‘handled’ everything that happened. No scenes that will blow your mind.<br><br>Other than that, I did enjoy this, really. I wasn’t that disappointed, since I did not have very high expectations, being one of the few who were not mesmerized by the ‘awesomeness’ (as many say) of the Legend trilogy. I enjoyed it, same as this one, but nothing more…<br><br>There was almost no romance. A little, but this is definitely not driven by romance. When it was present though, I was hooked and hold my breath at how captivating it was. But, like I said, there’s isn’t much of it. What a shame.<br><br>The writing was good and pleasant enough to read. I did think that the world-building wasn’t as developed as there was possibility to be though. The author did a great job at creating unforgettable characters but, in my opinion, she kind of neglected the world-building. There is some of it, of course, but you can see how the characters are more important compared to it.<br><br>When I think about how the author switched from dystopian (with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9275658.Legend__Legend___1_" title="Legend (Legend, #1) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">Legend</a>) to fantasy, (with this) I think she overall proved that she can create a story, whatever the genre will be. And that’s fantastic! Bravo to her! Would love to see if she pulls contemporary off. I think she could.<br><br>I would recommend this to fantasy fans out there. Be warned, though, it is very different from her well-known trilogy. You may see similarities to characters but, other than that, it’s completely different. It was a good read, some scenes were dragging here and there or having too much of Adelina’s internal struggles but it was engaging enough and the magic interesting.<br><br>PS. Am I the only one who thinks the cover is a little…cheap? Giving the impression that the design as a whole is only half finished? What are <i>your</i> thoughts on it?<br><br>Sources:<br>-<a href="http://www.tumblr.com/search/the%20young%20elites%20by%20marie%20lu" rel="nofollow noopener">First art</a><br>-<a href="http://www.pinterest.com/mreefish/the-young-elites/" rel="nofollow noopener">Second art</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7520876208118036117" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2054083051" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2054083051" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2054083051?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale?shelf=fantasy-series">fantasy-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2054083051" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer342549628342923001"><i>”His words remind me of the strange whispers that have accompanied my illusions – something dark and vengeful, tempting and powerful. A weight presses on my chest. I am afraid. Intrigued.”</i><br/><br/>As it seems <b>2018</b> is not only the year in which I’ll finally finish a few series I’ve been reading for years, but also the year in which I hand out my v-card to new authors I’ve never read before. *lol*<br/><br/>Last week it was Holly Black’s <b>“The Darkest Part of the Forest”</b> this week its Marie Lu’s <b>“The Young Elites”</b> and</span>
  <span id="freeText342549628342923001" style="display:none"><i>”His words remind me of the strange whispers that have accompanied my illusions – something dark and vengeful, tempting and powerful. A weight presses on my chest. I am afraid. Intrigued.”</i><br /><br />As it seems <b>2018</b> is not only the year in which I’ll finally finish a few series I’ve been reading for years, but also the year in which I hand out my v-card to new authors I’ve never read before. *lol*<br /><br />Last week it was Holly Black’s <b>“The Darkest Part of the Forest”</b> this week its Marie Lu’s <b>“The Young Elites”</b> and after reading both books I can say that I regret nothing! XD <br />I really liked this book, yet to write a decent review somehow seems to be so very difficult. I don’t know why I feel this way but I think it might be the same problem I had with Maas’s “Throne of Glass”. You just feel that it’s a debut novel and there were some flaws that make it kind of hard to write an elaborate review. Does that even make sense? No? For me neither! *lol*<br /><br />I guess what I’m trying to say is that I loved the characters! They were so grey and complex and I would have loved to dive a little deeper into their thoughts. But unfortunately Adelina’s POV was the only one that actually ran like a golden thread through the story. Sure, we got a little glimpse at Enzo’s, Teren’s and Raffaele’s POV as well, but overall I really would have enjoyed to read a little more of them. I think in some way those brief and few chapters only made me even more curious about them and left me kind of unsatisfied which is actually sad, because there was so much potential in those characters!!! XD I really hope Marie Lu tackles that in the second book and gives us more insight into their lives and backstories!<br /><br /><i>”Something blackens your heart, something deep and bitter. It has festered inside you for years, nurtured and encouraged. I’ve never felt anything like it.”</i><br /><br />I think another thing I missed and which wasn’t all too clearly portrayed was the world in which they live. I mean yes, we are informed that there are Malfettos and Elites and at the beginning of the book we even have a map, when it came down to describing their environment I could never really grasp the idea though. The picture of the Fortunata Court is still vague in my head and I’m afraid it will only get even vaguer the more time passes after finishing the book. *lol* That’s just my subtle opinion though so don’t let that keep you from reading <b>“The Young Elites”</b> because I’m sure it will get better with every book that’s following! ;-) <br /><br /><i>”I will be whispered about. I will have enemies lurking in every shadow. <br />Let them talk. Let their fear of me grow. I welcome it.”</i><br /><br />Well, and last but not least I have to point out the romance and diversity! *LOL* <u>We don’t only have people of every skin colour and with obvious flaws or different appearances but we also seem to have a nice LGBTQ representation!!!</u> Which of course, was enough to make yours truly a more than just happy woman! &lt;333 Haha! <br /><br />And speaking of which: Is it just me or does anyone else ship Enzo and Raffaele?! I mean I know we’re obviously supposed to ship Adelina and Enzo but I really didn’t feel anything between them… Not at all! Their scenes seemed to be so forced and if anything their ambitions seemed to be the main reason they were so drawn to each other. Enzo and Raffaele on the other hand?! Gosh you could feel their chemistry in every single line. They had about two moments but boy were they more intense than the ones with Adelina. *LOL* There was not even the slightest hint at a romance between those two boys but for me they somehow worked better than the official love interest?! I guess that’s again something that doesn’t make sense, but it is the way it is. XD<br /><br />Also I think this is the right moment to mention that I absolutely <b>love and adore Raffaele! &lt;333</b> He’s the secret star of the show and I loved the dynamics between him and the other characters. Especially Adelina and Enzo of course! ;-P I really hope to see even more of him in the next book and hopefully his POV will be represented again as well. =)<br /><br />Did I miss anything? Yes, Teren!!! I hate him… <u>strongly, deeply, intensely!</u>*lol* But he’s an awesome villain and I can’t wait to see what happened to him that changed him so profoundly! I’m sure there’s so much more than initially meets the eye and I can’t wait to read about his past! I already know this is going to be more than just interesting. =)))<br /><br /><i>”The rush of darkness through me is intoxicating and irresistible, and I find myself embracing it, letting it cover my insides like ink. Such power over these little masses. I love it.”</i><br /><br /><b>The bottom line:</b><br /><br />I loved to read <b>“The Young Elites”</b> and I can’t wait to read <b>“The Rose Society”</b>! Especially because the prologue was so freaking intriguing!!! That was a nice move Marie Lu, to introduce new characters at the end of the book. ;-P AND I’m really curious about: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Maeve and Lucent!!! Is there really going to be some f/f action in the second book because if yes: I ALREADY SHIP IT!!! &lt;333 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />All things considered: Happy Reading! I’m sure you won’t regret it! XD</span>
  <a data-text-id="342549628342923001" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2358873134" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10967751719231857995">Still waiting for a hyped ya series that won't disappoint me..<br/><br/>I seriously don't get why people say the protagonist is an anti hero. She literally is a typical ya fantasy protagonist that tries too hard to be dark and twisted. It's hella annoying.<br/>The other characters were pretty boring and I can't even remember their names lol. <br/>There wasn't much backstory to any of them except for the main character. I hope there will be more in the second & third book. <br/><br/>The plot itself wasn't very original, there</span>
  <span id="freeText10967751719231857995" style="display:none">Still waiting for a hyped ya series that won't disappoint me..<br /><br />I seriously don't get why people say the protagonist is an anti hero. She literally is a typical ya fantasy protagonist that tries too hard to be dark and twisted. It's hella annoying.<br />The other characters were pretty boring and I can't even remember their names lol. <br />There wasn't much backstory to any of them except for the main character. I hope there will be more in the second &amp; third book. <br /><br />The plot itself wasn't very original, there just wasn't anything new about it. <br />Additionally, I can't get into details because of spoilers, but there was a plot point which I generally dislike a lot. That's not necessarily a bad thing about the book, only a personal preference. <br /><br />This still gets 2* because I really enjoyed the writing style. The descriptions of the town, the clothes, the illusions, etc. were very detailed without being boring. It was really easy to picture the scenes inside of my head. Probs to Marie Lu. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1024682546" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8286130275730868827"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439391768i/15829778._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b><u>Edit 03/23</u> : There's no denying that I was disappointed in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20821111.The_Young_Elites__The_Young_Elites___1_' title='The Young Elites (The Young Elites, #1) by Marie Lu' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Young Elites</a>, <i>but</i> I thought I'd point that I absolutely loved <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23846013.The_Rose_Society__The_Young_Elites___2_' title='The Rose Society (The Young Elites, #2) by Marie Lu' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Rose Society</a>, its sequel. So, you know, fellow minority readers - I hope it will be the same for you^^</b><br/><br/>► <u>My review of book 2</u> : <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1584314178' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Rose Society</a> ★★★★★<br/><br/><b>
  <u>ORIGINAL REVIEW</u>
</b><br/><br/>Hey YOU! BOOK! <b>You pretended to be right up my alley!</b> You said I will love you! You said you were dark and captivating! <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439390106ra/15829536.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The truth is, after getting off to a flying start, the tension loosened more and mor</span>
  <span id="freeText8286130275730868827" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439391768i/15829778._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b><u>Edit 03/23</u> : There's no denying that I was disappointed in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20821111.The_Young_Elites__The_Young_Elites___1_" title="The Young Elites (The Young Elites, #1) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">The Young Elites</a>, <i>but</i> I thought I'd point that I absolutely loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23846013.The_Rose_Society__The_Young_Elites___2_" title="The Rose Society (The Young Elites, #2) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rose Society</a>, its sequel. So, you know, fellow minority readers - I hope it will be the same for you^^</b><br><br>► <u>My review of book 2</u> : <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1584314178" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rose Society</a> ★★★★★<br><br><b>
  <u>ORIGINAL REVIEW</u>
</b><br><br>Hey YOU! BOOK! <b>You pretended to be right up my alley!</b> You said I will love you! You said you were dark and captivating! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439390106ra/15829536.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The truth is, after getting off to a flying start, the tension loosened more and more, making the next 300 pages a real <i>core</i> to read for me. When I first met Adelina, I was ecstatic : because of the darkness that seemed to lie in her heart, she appeared to be the kind of morally ambiguous character I could root for. <br><br><b>Too bad the whole book turned out to be completely anticlimactic : I. WAS. BORED.</b> <br> <br>✘ <b>I don't like Mari Lu's writing</b> : I wouldn't be able to point what was wrong, exactly, but I kept feeling that something wasn't quite right with it. Frankly, I think that the present tense throws me off guard. And her sentences seemed... weird to me sometimes, bugging me so much that I had to reread them. It didn't <i>flow</i> smoothly. Not in my opinion anyway.<br><br>✘ Let's forget the fact that <b>there's barely any world-building</b>, except a re-creation of the Renaissance Italy with the black plague as an explication to the Young Elites new powers. Frankly, I'm okay with authors using real settings to create their fantasy world (take Mark Lawrence for example, whose Broken Empire is nothing more than Europe after an atomic war). However, if Mark Lawrence plays with this real background, letting the reader know where his inspiration lies, Mari Lu merely uses entire settings without never acknowledging what she borrowed. Changing names isn't enough. Is it high fantasy? No. It's alternate history with fantastic elements. <br><br>✘ <b>The pacing was <s>uneven</s> a big fail</b> : after a strong beginning which put my feelings all over the place, nothing really happens during several chapters.... until we start a new cycle again : an amazing scene and then boring pages during which I don't really know what to think. Like, the consort pages. What's the point? <br><br>While I desperately wanted to feel something, to feel captivated, I was drowned in descriptions of clothes and other useless details. For real, how many times do I have to read the word velvet? Huh? Take <s>Gabriele</s> <b>I meant <u>Raphaele</u>, and yes, I can confuse a character's name AND having read the book. <i>Please. Don't be ridiculous.</i></b> for example. I don't need to know everything he's wearing every day. Call me shallow, but I don't care.<br><br>✘ <b>This book is... <i>putdownable</i></b>. Is that a thing? (apparently, no, but I'll make it a thing, because I can) Indeed I kept feeling distracted during my read and before I could think more about it I was doing something else entirely (laundry, watching TV, just name it). <b>As far as my investment in the story is concerned, it's a big huge fail for me</b>.<br><br>✘ But <b>my biggest disappointment is Adelina</b>. I expected dark. I expected complex. That's absolutely not what I got. Let's get this straight : I love antiheroes. I have no problem to adore characters who are complete little shit and who embrace evil as a living. I crave them, for crying out loud, because good (haha) antiheroes are rare and complicated to create : how to make the readers root for a character whose actions disgust and disturb them? I have no clue, but when it's well-done, it's amazing. <b>Adelina... wasn't quite like that</b>. She is NOT an antihero but spends her time whining about events that aren't even her fault. Okay, okaaaay, she <i>thinks</i> about killing people and keeps telling us that there's a darkness inside her but frankly? BRING IT, GIRL. Stop whining and show me that there's more to you than your internal confusion. I was ready to accept EVERYTHING from her : jealousy, selfishness, murder instincts, betrayal, everything. <b>What I got is a lot of TELLING but not near enough SHOWING to make me care about her. I didn't.</b> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439349205i/15825170._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And you know what happens when I don't care about the characters?<br><br>It becomes a core to finish. <br><br>✘ <b>I didn't feel anything towards Enzo</b> as well except during his first apparition (what? I'm an Assassin's Creed whore and my eyes sparkle at the mention of daggers, don't mind me). <br><br>✘ To be frank, during most of the book I got the impression that <b>the characters were... wandering... to go.... somewhere... I think... It lacked directions and the plot was almost non-existent</b>, except for the betrayal trope I see in every Fantasy YA book I read these days. Look, it was a trope I used to love, and I still do, when it's executed properly, when it's more than an easy way to bring angst in a story. Sadly, in my opinion it belonged to the second category : I simply COULDN'T FEEL Adelina's struggles. Oh, she tells us. Well, she tells us a lot of things. But to me neither Teren nor Violetta felt like real characters, therefore I was never moved by this situation. Heavy sigh.<br><br>✔ <b>The ending, though?</b> <u>It was good</u>. It was everything I wanted from the book. It came... too late. How am I supposed to savor epic scenes if I haven't given a fuck about the characters for pages and pages? Why using most of the book as a set-up for a shocking ending? It feels just... cheap to me. A genuinely great ending won't make me forget that I was bored to death during 300 pages. Nope. Sorry.<br><br><b>This book didn't quite give me what it was telling me</b>. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439391768ra/15829779.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="8286130275730868827" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

And Marie Lu isn't afraid to take bold decisions here, oh yes.<br/><br/><u>Cons</u>: the writing. It feels lifeless, like a fellow classmate reading out a scene from your school literature book; you're hearing it, you're understanding it, but you're not really <i>fe</i></span>
  <span id="freeText12890663898720189752" style="display:none">I've never had such mixed feelings about a book before.<br /><br />Bloody hell. <br /><br /><u>Pros</u>: it's in the POV of an innocent victim-turned-antihero-turned-villian, which is something you just don't get enough of in the young adult realm (or at least that I've come across). And Marie Lu isn't afraid to take bold decisions here, oh yes.<br /><br /><u>Cons</u>: the writing. It feels lifeless, like a fellow classmate reading out a scene from your school literature book; you're hearing it, you're understanding it, but you're not really <i>feeling</i> it. And if a story's missing that vital component, then you might as well just be scanning ink printed over pages.<br /><br />NONETHELESS, I'm eager to see what becomes of Adelina and her gradual road to evil...or will she?<br />___________________________________<br /><br /><b>Book Song: <i>Exhile</i> by Eastghost.</b><br />___________________________________</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1779883635" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1779883635" />
    <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson"><img alt="✨    jamieson   ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499961431p2/7706640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1779883635?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨    jamieson   ✨" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson">✨    jamieson   ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1779883635" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7137698334548552453"><i>
  <blockquote>“Some hate us, think us outlaws to hang at the gallows.<br/> Some fear us, think us demons to burn at the stake.<br/> Some worship us, think us children of the gods. <br/>But all know us. </blockquote>
</i><br/><br/><br/><b>HOLY SHIT</b> this book was <i>that fucking good y'all</i><br/><br/>iM SHOOK<br/>im so damn SHOOK<br/><br/>This is the first book I've read in AGES where I've been genuinely thrilled about the plot ? where I've been so excited to know what happens next. I couldn't put this down ?? I'm so happy ??<br/><br/>everything about it is just .... amazing. the story, the compl</span>
  <span id="freeText7137698334548552453" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>“Some hate us, think us outlaws to hang at the gallows.<br> Some fear us, think us demons to burn at the stake.<br> Some worship us, think us children of the gods. <br>But all know us. </blockquote>
</i><br><br><br><b>HOLY SHIT</b> this book was <i>that fucking good y'all</i><br><br>iM SHOOK<br>im so damn SHOOK<br><br>This is the first book I've read in AGES where I've been genuinely thrilled about the plot ? where I've been so excited to know what happens next. I couldn't put this down ?? I'm so happy ??<br><br>everything about it is just .... amazing. the story, the complex characters, the world, the plot, the action, THE FACT IT'S A VILLAINS JOURNEY !!! the anti-hero's and general greyness of the characters, PLOT TWISTS, oh and it's super diverse and aaaaaaaaaaahhh<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1480385818ra/21303370.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>IM SO SHOOK I AM REELING FROM THAT ENDING I NEED THE NEXT BOOK .. IMMEDIATELY !!<br><br>~ ~ ~ ~ ~~ ~ ~ ~<br><br><b>DAYS</b> have passed since I wrote this mess of a post-reading review on this book and my <i>thoughts have not changed !!</i>. I'm still so shook<br><br>Since 2017 began I haven't <b>loved</b> anything I read. I mean it was okay, but there were no books which made my heart rush, which had me DYING to know the end. This book did. I was doing that thing where you peek at the end of the chapter because you must know (anD THEN SPOIL YOURSELF), and I stayed up sooo late to finish it. It was so damn exciting, I was <b>completely hooked</b> on this book, seriously, un-put-down-able. <br><br>I mean ? How could it not be. <br><br>Kids with superpowers ? Check. <br>Unstable government that must be overthrown by the rebellion ? Check. <br>A squad of friends ? Check. <br>A cast of anti-hero's who do bad things for the ''greater good'' ? Check. <br><br>I WAS BOUND TO LOVE IT. <br><br><br><i>
  <blockquote>“I am tired of being used, hurt, and cast aside. It is my turn to use. My turn to hurt.”</blockquote>
</i><br><br><b>NOTE ABOUT THIS BOOK:</b> absolutely <i>none</i> of these characters are good people. Even the ones I thought were decent turned out to be shit. there some serious villainous mfs over here. <br><br>The characters were the absolute highlight !! Each was incredible complex and nuanced, each was built up on those murky grey lines, every single character had aspects of their personality that made them the anti-hero, but every single one thought themselves the hero. I adored this characterisation, on a character level but also as a depiction of humanity. We aren't all good or all bad, we're all somewhere in the middle. <br><br>The beautiful thing about this villainy though is that it isn't in your face - it's perfectly, gorgeously subtle. It's just a lie here and there, it's people pretending and hiding their true thoughts, it's gently befriending someone just to use them. The thing that had me so SHOOK was even I was convinced, even me, who got to see from multiple points of view thought some things that turned out to be fake were real. I was also caught up in the lies and the manipulation. <br><br><b>I LOVED</b> that the main character is a girl who just got pushed a little too far. A girl who's been abused and manipulated and shunned and who is now getting back, who's rising above it, who's been turned hard and cruel by the world. Adelina is an incredible interesting character with many nuances and complexities AND I CAN'T WAIT FOR HER TO RISE IN THE ROSE SOCIETY. <br><br><i>
  <blockquote>“I hereby pledge to serve the Dagger Society, to strike fear into the hearts of those who rule Kenettra, to take by death what belong to us, and to make the power of our Elites known to every man, woman, and child. Should I break my vow, let the dagger take from me what I took from the dagger.” </blockquote>
</i> <br><br><b>
  <u>Other good points</u>
</b> <br><br>SUCH. GOOD. REPRESENTATION !!!!!<br><br>Many, many people of colour !!!!! lgbt rep !!!!! characters with physical flaws which they use to their advantage !!!!! <br><br>Soo twisty turny, !! never guessed where it was going next and reveals and plot points which genuinely shocked me. <br><br>good romance !! not too much of it but an interesting romance and one which, like the characters, is complex, built upon ambition and lust for power (perhaps) more then love. <br><br>AWESOME super powers !! I'm always like, super powers are boring sometimes because there's no diversity in the powers but nooo I really liked these ones ! <br><br>~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~<br><br>Honestly, this book was just super intense and fun !! Gave me lots of six of crows vibes and overrall was just really good. I was so, so engaged and immersed with this world and these characters I've literally been dreaming about how good it's gonna be when I can start Rose Society <b>I LOVE THIS</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="7137698334548552453" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
